## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting stress (sigma) from strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a core problem in constitutive modeling of materials. The relationship captures elastic and plastic deformation, strain hardening, and thermal softening or expansion effects typical in solid mechanics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic behavior)
- Thermo-elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (linear stress including thermal expansion/contribution)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic hardening)
- Ludwik yield and hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress followed by power-law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (stress saturating towards an ultimate value)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening reduced exponentially by temperature)
- Power-law with linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (hardening with linear temperature dependence)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (yield, hardening, and temperature effect combined multiplicatively)
- Parabolic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * sqrt(epsilon) (stress scaling with square root of strain, dislocation-based)
- Sigmoidal transition: sigma = c0 / (1 + exp(-c1 * (epsilon - c2))) * exp(c3 * T) (smooth elastic-plastic transition with thermal softening)
- Thermal strain influence: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T)**c2 (stress with thermal strain offset)
- Combined saturation and softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening reduced by temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain: a term c0 * epsilon indicates a direct linear elastic response.
- Constant stress offset: an additive constant c in sigma = c + ... represents a yield strength or initial internal stress.
- Power-law strain term: epsilon**c with c between 0 and 1 suggests strain hardening typical of plastic deformation.
- Saturation of stress: 1 - exp(-c * epsilon) models stress approaching a maximum (exponential hardening saturation).
- Exponential temperature factor: exp(c * T) or exp(-c * T) often captures thermal softening or thermal activation.
- Multiplicative decomposition: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) indicates the effects of strain and temperature are decoupled.
- Additive temperature term: sigma = f(epsilon) + c * T models thermo-elastic stress due to thermal expansion.
- Negative linear temperature coefficient: factor (1 - c * T) is a simple linear thermal softening model.
- Square root strain: epsilon**0.5 or sqrt(epsilon) corresponds to parabolic hardening from dislocation theory.
- Sigmoid in strain: a logistic or tanh function in epsilon models a smooth transition from elastic to plastic flow.
